[<p>They say all the stereotypical symbols of romance, like a diamond, are forever \u2014 but some couples seem to be beyond the outward appearances of love, or, at least, the stereotypical ones you might expect. Jada <a class="" href="https://people.com/movies/jada-pinkett-smith-will-dont-celebrate-wedding-anniversaries/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Pinkett Smith says she and Will Smith don't celebrate</a> their wedding anniversary in a typical way, and you know what? It's totally OK, because that's what works for them. </p>, <p>As <em>People </em>reported, Pinkett Smith, 47, and Smith, 50, marked their 22nd wedding anniversary on Dec. 31. But that doesn't mean the longtime couple pulled out all the stops and went for the usual symbols of domestic bliss such as red roses, dinner out, or fancy jewelry.</p>, <p> In fact, it's not even clear whether the couple was in the same city at the time of their anniversary. </p>, <p>The actress noted in Monday, Dec. 31's episode of <a class="" href="https://www.facebook.com/redtabletalk/?tn-str=k*F" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><em>Red Table Talk</em> on Facebook </a>that she and her superstar hubby don't really go in for the whole anniversary thing. Which is 100 percent fine by her. </p>, <p>"We don\u2019t really celebrate that day anymore in that sense, because the context of our union is totally different. Usually, Will on New Year\u2019s likes to be in an adventure in the world somewhere. There\u2019s no telling where he\u2019s gonna be. And I like to be inside. I don\u2019t wanna be out in the world. He now has the freedom to go and have an awesome adventure of some kind."</p>, <p>In fact, <a class="" href="https://www.facebook.com/redtabletalk/videos/2184223845174527/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Pinkett Smith's newest video, posted on their anniversary</a>, mainly covers fitness and Pinkett Smith's internal search for self-love and meaning. The show, which as <em>The Hollywood Reporter</em> noted, typically features the couple's daughter, <a class="" href="https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/jada-pinkett-smith-kicks-first-red-table-talk-1108862" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Willow Smith, and Pinkett Smith's mother, Adrienne Banfield Norris</a>, features three generations of women indulging in totally open dialogue.</p>, <p>But before you make any assumptions about the Pinkett Smith marriage \u2014 they met when he was starring in <em>The Fresh Prince of Bel-Air, </em>they explained on air \u2014 the stars sat down in a recent episode for <a class="" href="https://www.facebook.com/redtabletalk/videos/2174148442809253/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">straight talk about their relationship</a> and family life. </p>, <p>The pair, who married in Baltimore on Dec. 31, 1997 and also share son Jaden, 20, as<em> People </em>confirmed, noted on the show that their version of "happily ever after" hasn't come without a lot of emotional work. </p>, <p>Pinkett Smith and Smith got together on the heels of Smith's divorce, they revealed, and awhile after that, Pinkett Smith found herself pregnant and reluctantly and angrily planning a fancy wedding with morning sickness. (Something which her mom apologizes for insisting on during the conversation.)</p>, <p>"'Til death do us part,' is real for me, but all the rules and ideas ... The accepted conventional definition of 'wife?' ... I'm not that," Pinkett Smith added before Smith noted that he credits most of his success to being married to Pinkett Smith and her demand he always do his best.</p>, <p>"The thing with the two of us that never got out is the intention. We were always in sync on a couple of really powerful ideas. We were always building a family, that was our number one priority, family ... As a couple, we are magical," Smith noted.</p>, <p>Of course, Pinkett Smith's candid Facebook conversations have covered a lot more than her marriage, including a recent episode in which she interviewed <em>Grey's Anatomy</em>'s <a class="" href="https://www.romper.com/p/ellen-pompeo-candidly-discusses-raising-biracial-kids-on-red-table-talk-15504965">Ellen Pompeo about raising biracial kids. </a>But the star's outlook on marriage is refreshing in a social media culture in which it can sometimes seem like most couples are trying to look better than the next. </p>, <p>\u201c[My relationship] is more of a life partnership, so it\u2019s not steeped in marital, in that day,\u201d <a class="" href="https://www.facebook.com/redtabletalk/?tn-str=k*F" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Pinkett Smith said on the show.</a> I love the honesty, and the fact that this duo not only does things its own way, but that they've made it work so well for so long.</p>, <p><b><em>After a very frustrating first birth experience, this Deaf mother wanted a change. Will the help of two Deaf doulas give the quality communication and birth experience this mom wants and deserves? Watch Episode Four of Romper's </em>Doula Diaries, Season Two<em>, below, and visit </em><a class="" href="https://www.youtube.com/user/EliteDaily" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><em>Bustle Digital Group's YouTube page</em></a><em> for more episodes.</em></b></p>]
[<p class="byline__name byline__name--block">\n<a data-metrics='{"action":"Click Byline","category":"Story Metadata"}' href="https://www.npr.org/people/2100593/terry-gross" rel="author">\n      Terry Gross\n    </a>\n</p>, <p><a data-metrics='{"action":"Click Org Association","category":"Story Metadata"}' href="http://www.npr.org/programs/fresh-air/"><img alt="Fresh Air" src="https://media.npr.org/chrome/ext_provider_427869011.gif"/></a></p>, <p>\n                Christian Bale stars as Dick Cheney in <em>Vice</em>. The film, which was written and directed by Adam McKay, has been nominated for six Golden Globe Awards.\n                \n                <b aria-label="Image credit" class="credit">\n                    \n                    Greig Fraser/Annapurna Pictures\n                    \n                </b>\n<b class="hide-caption"><b>hide caption</b></b>\n</p>, <p class="caption">Christian Bale stars as Dick Cheney in <em>Vice</em>. The film, which was written and directed by Adam McKay, has been nominated for six Golden Globe Awards.</p>, <p>Former Vice President <a href="https://www.npr.org/tags/128526156/vice-president-dick-cheney">Dick Cheney</a> was the quintessential behind-the-scenes political power player. "He really has no signature speech \u2014 there's no great Dick Cheney moment where he was in front of a pulpit delivering a great line," says filmmaker Adam McKay. "He's always kind of just been in the background."</p>, <p>McKay aims to bring the powerful former vice president into the foreground in his new film, <em>Vice,</em> a dark comedy starring Christian Bale. The movie<em> </em>combines the work of investigative journalists with some speculation and comedy (McKay also directed <em>Anchorman </em>and<em> </em><a href="https://www.npr.org/2015/12/11/459344815/on-the-money-how-the-big-short-and-its-jerk-heroes-explain-finance">The Big Short</a>) to tell the story of Cheney's ascent from Yale dropout to West Wing operative under former President George W. Bush.</p>, <p>"I think a lot of the ways that people like Cheney have gained power is that they rely on us being bored. They rely on us looking at what they do and assuming that it's just bureaucracy and who cares?" McKay says. But "when you really dig into it, it's very exciting stuff. And it's major stuff that changes the world."</p>, <p><strong>On Cheney's legacy </strong></p>, <p>The biggest thing he did was by going to war [in Iraq]<strong> </strong>, and then in the end [it] turned out the intelligence was bogus, which I think [whether] you're right-wing or left-wing, I think you have to agree that was the case, and how America just moved on from that. I think at that point we started to get comfortable with the fact that our government wasn't entirely working for us, and that there were agendas inside our government that didn't represent the will of the people.</p>, <p>So I think in an abstract sense, he changed the way we view government, but then, in a very tangible sense \u2014 I mean, let's face it \u2014 the Middle East became completely destabilized. You had the rise of ISIS. They tripled the debt, and then obviously the world economy collapsed. And they were really the first administration who nakedly put lobbyists and corporate insiders in regulatory jobs.</p>, <p><strong>On a turning point in Cheney's life, after he dropped out of Yale, when he moved back to Wyoming and stopped drinking because of his girlfriend, Lynne, who later became his wife</strong></p>, <p>He was working as a [power] lineman in Wyoming. We're talking the early '60s. That's a tough, tough town, a tough state to work in, and what would happen is they would work on the lines all day. They would climb up and put up the power ... and then at night they would go out and they would drink, like old-fashioned, 19th century drinking. He got a couple DUIs. ...</p>, <p>He loved Lynne Vincent from the second he saw her. ... He was crazy about her. [After she confronted him about his drinking,] he white-knuckled it. ... He stopped going into town at night and he stayed in this little crappy trailer with an old World War I veteran, and he would sit there and they would eat, like, canned tuna fish and Dick would ask him stories about World War I, and that's how he stopped getting into trouble and then eventually got back into college.</p>, <p><strong>On the musical number cut from the movie </strong></p>, <p>It was so good. We had <a href="https://www.npr.org/2016/01/28/464631594/alabama-shakes-brittany-howard-on-small-town-life-big-time-music">Brittany Howard</a> from the Alabama Shakes. We had the choreographer of <em>Hamilton</em>. We had Christian Bale and [Steve] Carell. ... It was amazing. It just tonewise and storywise did not work in that part of the film, and we tried and tried and tried. It almost worked. I've had a little pang recently, "Man, maybe I should have just left that in there," but the good news is, it will be out ... when the release of the movie happens and streaming and DVD and all that kind of stuff, and it really is tremendous.</p>, <p>\n                Director Adam McKay (from left), actor Christian Bale, producer Kevin Messick and cinematographer Greig Fraser discuss a scene on the set of <em>Vice</em>.\n                \n                <b aria-label="Image credit" class="credit">\n                    \n                    Matt Kennedy/Annapurna Pictures\n                    \n                </b>\n<b class="hide-caption"><b>hide caption</b></b>\n</p>, <p class="caption">Director Adam McKay (from left), actor Christian Bale, producer Kevin Messick and cinematographer Greig Fraser discuss a scene on the set of <em>Vice</em>.</p>, <p><strong>On Cheney's heart issues </strong></p>, <p>At one point he had ... basically a little jump-starter in his heart so when he would have a heart attack it would give his heart a kick to keep it alive and it had like a little computer in it. ...</p>, <p>I think he had five heart attacks, but if you count the transplant [in 2012], if you count the device they put in ... it's kind of hard to calculate, but during the 1970s when he was working in the Ford administration, the youngest chief of staff in history, he was smoking three packs of cigarettes a day and eating a dozen doughnuts every day, so clearly not treating his heart that well.</p>, <p><strong>On McKay's own recent heart attack </strong></p>, <p>We had just finished filming, I think we had wrapped for about a week, and ... I just realized I was not in the best shape. I put on weight during the movie. I was foolish enough to continue smoking ... and I didn't feel good. ...</p>, <p>I was working out with my trainer and in the middle of it my hands started tingling and my stomach felt queasy. Those aren't normally symptoms you think of with a heart attack. You usually think of pain in the chest, in the arm. So I told my trainer, "I'm fine. I'm fine. I'm just tired. This is just weird." And he left, and as soon as he left I remembered the heart attack scene we shot with Bale when [Cheney] was running for Congress in Wyoming in the late '70s and Bale asked me, "How do you want to do the heart attack? Do you want it to be a pain in the arm? The chest?" He goes, "I could also do the queasy stomach. That's really common." ...</p>, <p>And so that moment just [flashed back] to me while I was sitting on the couch and I went, "Holy Lord!" and I ran upstairs ... and I just downed four baby aspirin and called 911. ... The doctor said, "Because you acted so quickly you have no damage to your heart." ... So I called Christian Bale a week later and I said, "Either you or Dick Cheney just saved my life."</p>, <p><strong>On how that experience changed him </strong></p>, <p>I definitely started talking to [Will] Ferrell about maybe we have to get back in the saddle again and do a big old comedy, because there's just no better way to spend your life than, like, laughing every single day.</p>, <p class="byline">Director Adam McKay</p>, <p>When I came out of the heart attack, I just had the biggest, dumbest smile on my face for like a week, where I could not stop joking around. I was so happy to be alive and what it does is it \u2014 for me, personally \u2014 just reaffirms what you care about and there's a lot of things I love in life, but one of the things I love in life is laughing \u2014 laughing really hard. ...</p>, <p>It did make me miss the comedy, I got to be honest. It did make me feel that like, maybe there's something to be said about if you can come up with a raucously funny movie that there's just something about that's just undeniable. So I definitely started talking to [Will] Ferrell about maybe we have to get back in the saddle again and do another big old comedy, because there's just no better way to spend your life than, like, laughing every single day.</p>, <p><em>Heidi Saman and Thea Chaloner produced and edited this interview for broadcast. Bridget Bentz, Molly Seavy-Nesper and Beth Novey adapted it for the Web.</em></p>, <p class="left">NPR thanks our sponsors</p>, <p class="right"><a href="/about-npr/186948703/corporate-sponsorship">Become an NPR sponsor</a></p>]
[<p><img alt="Coachella 2019" class="alignnone size-630scaled wp-image-387734" height="787" src="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/files/2019/01/coachella2019.jpg" width="630"/></p>, <p>Here we go: <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/coachella-2019-on-sale-this-week/">Coachella</a> has just announced its 2019 lineup. <strong>Childish Gambino, Tame Impala</strong>, and <strong>Ariana Grande</strong> headline this year, and the lineup also includes <strong>Janelle Monae, The 1975, Anderson .Paak &amp; The Free Nationals, Kacey Musgraves, Rosalia, Khruangbin, Charlotte Gainsbourg, SOPHIE, Tierra Whack, Beach Fossils, Yves Tumor, Kero Kero Bonito, Let\u2019s Eat Grandma, Turnstile, Solange, Kid Cudi, Weezer, Aphex Twin, J Balvin, Bassnectar, Four Tet, Christine and The Queens, Wiz Khalifa, Mac DeMarco, Sheck Wes, Ty Segall &amp; White Fence, Smino, Idris Elba, Hop Along, Shame, serpentwithfeet,</strong> <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/the-messthetics-ex-fugazi-prep-debut-for-dischord-listen-touring/">Fugazi offshoot</a> <strong>The Messthetics, Bad Bunny, CHVRCHES, YG, Playboi Carti, H.E.R., Blood Orange, Pusha T, Unknown Mortal Orchestra, Kaytranada, Jon Hopkins, Lizzo, SOB x RBE, Soccer Mommy, U.S. Girls, Men I Trust, Iceage, Turnover, Hurray for the Riff Raff, The Interrupters, Little Simz</strong>, and more. See the full lineup in the poster above.</p>, <p><strong>UPDATE:</strong> for the first time ever, <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/coachella-livestreaming-both-weekends-in-2019/">both weekends of Coachella will livestream</a> this year.</p>, <p>Visual artist Weirdcore <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/coachella-2019-rumors-kanye-west-out-aphex-twin-in/">teased</a> Aphex Twin\u2019s Coachella slot before it was announced. It\u2019ll be his third U.S. show in eleven years \u2013 the last two were Houston\u2019s <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/day-for-night-day-1-in-pics-aphex-twin-jamc-blood-orange-john-carpenter-more/">Day for Night festival</a> in 2016, and <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/more-pictures-f/">Coachella 2008</a>.</p>, <p>Both Tame Impala and Childish Gambino have been teasing new albums for a while. Do headlining Coachella slots mean 2019 will finally be the year they see the light of day?</p>, <p>For Ariana Grande, this is part of her massive <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/ariana-grande-announces-2019-tour-madison-square-garden-included/">2019 world tour</a> which also includes <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/tours-announced-mitski-ariana-grande-travis-barker-tyler-childers-monolord-more/">four arena shows in NYC</a>.</p>, <p>Most people know Idris Elba from his acting roles, including Stringer Bell in <em>The Wire</em>, John Luther in <em>Luther</em>, and various Marvel films, but he\u2019s also a <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/idris-elba-stringer-bell-launching-record-label-djing-in-brooklyn-this-week/">musician and DJ</a>, and he runs his own record label, <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/idris-elba-stringer-bell-launching-record-label-djing-in-brooklyn-this-week/">7Wallace Music</a>.</p>, <p>As we <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/coachella-2019-rumors-kanye-west-out-aphex-twin-in/">posted earlier</a>, Kanye West, who was <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/kanye-justin-timberlake-childish-gambino-headlining-coachella-2019/">rumored</a> to headline, allegedly dropped off the lineup because of disagreements with Goldenvoice over his stage setup. Justin Timberlake, who was also previously <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/kanye-justin-timberlake-childish-gambino-headlining-coachella-2019/">rumored</a> to headline, <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/tours-announced-justin-timberlake-ladytron-my-brightest-diamond-more/">rescheduled tour dates</a> after suffering damaged vocal cords, and isn\u2019t on the lineup, either.</p>, <p>This year marks\xa0the festival\u2019s 20th anniversary, and happens the consecutive weekends of\xa0<a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/coachella-2019-on-sale-this-week/">April 12-14\xa0and\xa0April 19-21</a> at Empire Polo Club in Indio, CA. <a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/coachella-2019-on-sale-this-week/">Presale tickets</a> are sold out, but <a href="https://coachella.com/buying-passes/">additional passes</a> go on sale Friday, January 4 at 11 AM PT.</p>, <p class="more_act"><a href="http://www.brooklynvegan.com/category/pictures/" title="More Galleries">More Galleries</a></p>, <p>\n\t\t\tIt appears that you already have an account created within our VIP network of sites on <a class="blog-tag generic-link-color" href="#"></a>.\n\t\t\tTo keep your personal information safe, we need to verify that it's really you.\n\t\t\tTo activate your account, please confirm your <a class="blog-tag generic-link-color" href="#"></a> password.\n\t\t\tWhen you have confirmed your password, you will be able to log in through Facebook on both sites.\n\t\t</p>, <p class="error-messages"></p>, <p>\n<label>Enter your password</label>\n<input class="password" name="cpwd" type="password" value=""/>\n<a class="forgot generic-link-color" href="/login/?action=lost-password">Forgot your password?</a>\n</p>, <p>It appears that you already have an account on this site associated with <strong class="user-email"></strong>. [<p class="Author__MyAuthor-f3kyos-0 sNryQ">By <strong><a href="https://honey.nine.com.au/meet-the-team/christine-estera">Christine Estera</a></strong><span>| <time datetime="2019-01-03T02:38:00.000Z" title="2019-01-03 02:38">22 hours ago</time></span></p>, <p><a href="https://celebrity.nine.com.au/ariel-winter" target="_blank"><strong><span>Ariel Winter</span></strong></a><span>'s 2019 has kicked off to a bad start.</span></p>, <p><span>The </span><em><span>Modern Family</span></em><span> actress was </span><a href="https://celebrity.nine.com.au/2018/07/08/12/42/ariel-winter-taking-a-break-from-twitter" target="_blank" title="taunted by social media trolls"><span>taunted by social media trolls</span></a><span> as she celebrated New Year's Eve in LA with her boyfriend, </span><strong><span>Levi Meaden</span></strong><span>. After the 20-year-old posted two photos of herself and the Canadian actor sharing a kiss at midnight, her followers felt the need to comment on everything from her weight loss to her alleged underage drinking.</span></p>, <p><span><div data-dump-id="Embed.1546563354585.2006781" data-mount="true" style="display:inline"><div data-component="Embed" style="display:inline"><div class="sc-EHOje hOovbw"></div></div><script id="Embed.1546563354585.2006781" type="text/base64">eyJ1cmwiOiJodHRwczpcdTAwMkZcdTAwMkZhcGkuaW5zdGFncmFtLmNvbVx1MDAyRm9lbWJlZD91cmw9aHR0cHMlM0ElMkYlMkZ3d3cuaW5zdGFncmFtLmNvbSUyRnAlMkZCc0hVT2dEQXUtVSUyRiZvbWl0c2NyaXB0PXRydWUmaGlkZWNhcHRpb249ZmFsc2UiLCJzY3JpcHQiOiJodHRwczpcdTAwMkZcdTAwMkZwbGF0Zm9ybS5pbnN0YWdyYW0uY29tXHUwMDJGZW5fVVNcdTAwMkZlbWJlZHMuanMiLCJwcm92aWRlciI6Imluc3RhZ3JhbSIsImVtYmVkIjpudWxsfQ==</script></div></span></p>, <p><span>"Drinking underage! <p><span>"Not half as bad as all the coke/meth she uses. She literally dropped 30 ponds [sic]," wrote on commenter.</span></p>, <p><figure><img sizes="(min-width: 1024px) 636px, (min-width: 768px) 396px, 100vw" src="https://imageresizer.static9.net.au/r1H7Lt7u-8qXcwXHS699b-FgRD0=/396x0/http%3A%2F%2Fprod.static9.net.au%2F_%2Fmedia%2F2019%2F01%2F03%2F13%2F32%2FAriel_Winter_responds_allegations_weight_loss_due_to_drugs.JPG" srcset="https://imageresizer.static9.net.au/r1H7Lt7u-8qXcwXHS699b-FgRD0=/396x0/http%3A%2F%2Fprod.static9.net.au%2F_%2Fmedia%2F2019%2F01%2F03%2F13%2F32%2FAriel_Winter_responds_allegations_weight_loss_due_to_drugs.JPG 396w, https://imageresizer.static9.net.au/M7GDrS3e8ts-wPePAK1TiRjsdrY=/636x0/http%3A%2F%2Fprod.static9.net.au%2F_%2Fmedia%2F2019%2F01%2F03%2F13%2F32%2FAriel_Winter_responds_allegations_weight_loss_due_to_drugs.JPG 636w, https://imageresizer.static9.net.au/oCLdqQBt6uuNMrBsJdPud3V4QCQ=/792x0/http%3A%2F%2Fprod.static9.net.au%2F_%2Fmedia%2F2019%2F01%2F03%2F13%2F32%2FAriel_Winter_responds_allegations_weight_loss_due_to_drugs.JPG 792w, https://imageresizer.static9.net.au/Ef6gzjVOtFhLbKk6WSHJil6JE_k=/1274x0/http%3A%2F%2Fprod.static9.net.au%2F_%2Fmedia%2F2019%2F01%2F03%2F13%2F32%2FAriel_Winter_responds_allegations_weight_loss_due_to_drugs.JPG 1274w"/><figcaption><span>(Instagram)</span></figcaption></figure></p>, <p><span>Winter wasn't going to let that remark slide either and sarcastically fired back, "Yup\u2026I dropped 30 bodies of water so fast\u2026 And yes!! [<p>SALT LAKE CITY \u2014 J.R.R. Tolkien would have celebrated his 126th birthday today.</p>, <p>"The Lord of the Rings\u201d author was born on Jan. 3, 1892, in the town of Bloemfontein, South Africa. He eventually moved to England, where he lived as a child, according to his biography.</p>, <p>He died in 1973 at age 81.</p>, <p>A <a href="https://www.reddit.com/comments/a9zke8">viral Reddit post last week</a> unveiled a rather interesting Easter egg about his death.</p>, <p>\u201cJ.R.R. Tolkien passed away in 1973,\u201d the Reddit user wrote. \u201cIf you reverse that number it is 3791. Three rings for the Elves. Seven for the Dwarves. Nine for Men. And one ring to rule them all.\u201d</p>, <p>This is a quick reference to an epigraph in the books that talk about the rings.</p>, <p><strong>The entire passage reads:</strong></p>, <p>"Three Rings for the Elven-kings under the sky, Seven for the Dwarf-lords in their halls of stone, Nine for Mortal Men doomed to die, One for the Dark Lord on his dark throne In the Land of Mordor where the Shadows lie. One Ring to rule them all, One Ring to find them, One Ring to bring them all and in the darkness bind them In the Land of Mordor where the Shadows lie."</p>, <p><strong>Birthday:</strong> Social media users celebrated Tolkien\u2019s birthday Thursday.</p>, <p dir="ltr" lang="en">Happy birthday to J. R. R. Tolkien, born today in 1892! Let's look back at a few classic book covers to celebrate... <a href="https://t.co/PN1yIowseY">pic.twitter.com/PN1yIowseY</a></p>, <p dir="ltr" lang="en">J. R. R. Tolkien was born on this day in 1892! We take a look back at one of The Lord of the Rings' most iconic moments on its creator's 127th birthday: <a href="https://t.co/Y3a7GEu0e8">https://t.co/Y3a7GEu0e8</a> <a href="https://t.co/lo85KchS1p">pic.twitter.com/lo85KchS1p</a></p>, <p dir="ltr" lang="en">END? No, the journey doesn't end here<br/>Death is just another path, one that we all must take<br/>The grey rain-curtain of this world rolls back, and all turns to silver glass<br/>'AND THEN YOU SEE IT'<br/>White shores, and beyond<br/>A far green country under a swift sunrise.<br/>    J. R .R. TOLKIEN <a href="https://t.co/T8bCW3zjdn">pic.twitter.com/T8bCW3zjdn</a></p>]

[<p>They're striking back \u2013 again.</p>, <p class="body-text">In what is undoubtedly the first piece of excellent news of 2019, Kevin Smith has confirmed that <em>Jay and</em> <em>Silent Bob Reboot </em>is in the works. </p>, <p class="body-text">Smith is developing the film \u2013 which is actually called <em>Reboot</em>, as opposed to being a reboot itself \u2013 with producer Jordan Monsanto, having previously teased it back in 2017. </p>, <p class="body-text">Spent the first day of 2019 having a <a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://twitter.com/hashtag/JayAndSilentBobReboot?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc^tfw" href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/JayAndSilentBobReboot?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#JayAndSilentBobReboot</a> pre-pre-production meeting at our holiday-roomy <a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://twitter.com/WeWork?ref_src=twsrc^tfw" href="https://twitter.com/WeWork?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@WeWork</a> office! <a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://twitter.com/JayMewes?ref_src=twsrc^tfw" href="https://twitter.com/JayMewes?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@JayMewes</a> took this pic of me and <a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://twitter.com/JordanMonsanto?ref_src=twsrc^tfw" href="https://twitter.com/JordanMonsanto?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@JordanMonsanto</a> to both mark the moment and to document that we were the only dopes in Hollywood working on the holiday. <a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://t.co/xTNrpN6OF6" href="https://t.co/xTNrpN6OF6">pic.twitter.com/xTNrpN6OF6</a></p>, <p class="body-text">On New Year's Day, Smith said in a tweet: "Spent the first day of 2019 having a #JayAndSilentBobReboot pre-pre-production meeting at our holiday-roomy @WeWork office.</p>, <p class="body-text">"@JayMewes took this pic of me and @JordanMonsanto to both mark the moment and to document that we were the only dopes in Hollywood working on the holiday."</p>, <p class="body-text">Jason Mewes and Smith first appeared as Jay and Silent Bob respectively in 1994's <em>Clerks</em>. They subsequently appeared in Smith's films <em>Mallrats</em>, <em>Chasing Amy</em> and <em><a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://www.digitalspy.com/movies/a839960/kevin-smith-dogma-2-rejection/" href="https://www.digitalspy.com/movies/a839960/kevin-smith-dogma-2-rejection/" target="_blank">Dogma</a></em>, before getting their very own spin-off, <em>Jay and Silent Bob Strike Back</em>, in 2001. </p>, <p class="body-text"> <a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://www.instagram.com/p/BQToHbElEhV/?utm_source=ig_embed&amp;utm_medium=loading" href="https://www.instagram.com/p/BQToHbElEhV/?utm_source=ig_embed&amp;utm_medium=loading" style=" color:#000; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; font-style:normal; font-weight:normal; line-height:17px; text-decoration:none; word-wrap:break-word;" target="_blank">This is not a drill! This is an actual image from my laptop! Yes, Kids - @jayandsilentbob are coming back! Here's the story: Sadly, Clerks III can't happen (one of our four leads opted out of the flick). So I worked on a #Mallrats movie instead... which also didn't happen because it turned into a #Mallrats series. I've pitched said sequel series to 6 different networks only to find no takers thus far. Mind you, I'm not complaining: nobody gets to make EVERYTHING they wanna make in this business (do they?). And I've been lucky to make anything at all, there's so much competition out there, so many much cooler ideas from fresh folks. And besides: I had #comicbookmen and then @tuskthemovie and @yogahosers (which all came together so crazy quickly), and the podcasts and #fatmanonbatman. With all of that, how could I bitch about no Clerks III or Mallrats 2? Then when I started directing @thecw shows, it was such a slice of Heaven on Earth, I happily put my Askewniverse sequels to the side. Since I sold #Clerks and #Mallrats years ago, they're owned by others, which limits my moves with my own material. I don't mind: back in the day, all I ever wanted to do was sell my stuff so I could be in the movie biz in the first place. So I don't own Clerks, Mallrats, Chasing Amy or #Dogma... But I DO own #jayandsilentbob. So while I love playing with someone else's new toys on @cwtheflash and @Supergirl, I'm getting eager to play with my old toys again in the inter-connected View Askewniverse I spent the first half of my career creating. And so all last month, I had the time of my life laughing while writing "Jay and Silent Bob Reboot" - a fun flick in which the Jersey boys have to go back to Hollywood to stop a brand new reboot of the old "Bluntman &amp; Chronic Movie" they hated so much. It's a tongue-in-cheek, silly-ass satire that pokes fun at the movie business's recent re-do obsession, featuring an all-star cast of cameos and familiar faces! And I already met with the good folks at Miramax and they're into it, so I'm hoping we'll be shooting in the summer! Never give up, kids. You CAN do anything you want in life, so long as you're patient and malleable. #KevinSmith</a></p>, <p class="body-text">A post shared by <a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://www.instagram.com/thatkevinsmith/?utm_source=ig_embed&amp;utm_medium=loading" href="https://www.instagram.com/thatkevinsmith/?utm_source=ig_embed&amp;utm_medium=loading" style=" color:#c9c8cd; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; font-style:normal; font-weight:normal; line-height:17px;" target="_blank"> Kevin Smith</a> (@thatkevinsmith) on <time datetime="2017-02-09T21:54:40+00:00" style=" font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px;">Feb 9, 2017 at 1:54pm PST</time></p>, <p class="body-text">Back in 2017, Smith <a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://www.digitalspy.com/movies/a820972/kevin-smith-jay-and-silent-bob-reboot-announcement/" href="https://www.digitalspy.com/movies/a820972/kevin-smith-jay-and-silent-bob-reboot-announcement/" target="_blank">revealed that he was writing </a><em><a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="https://www.digitalspy.com/movies/a820972/kevin-smith-jay-and-silent-bob-reboot-announcement/" href="https://www.digitalspy.com/movies/a820972/kevin-smith-jay-and-silent-bob-reboot-announcement/" target="_blank">Jay and Silent Bob Reboot</a></em>, a film that is essentially identical to the original and satirises the industry's recent 're-do obsession'.<br/></p>, <p class="body-text">He wrote in a post on Instagram: "Last month, I had the time of my life laughing while writing "Jay and Silent Bob Reboot" - a fun flick in which the Jersey boys have to go back to Hollywood to stop a brand new reboot of the old "Bluntman &amp; Chronic Movie" they hated so much. </p>, <p class="body-text">"It's a tongue-in-cheek, silly-ass satire that pokes fun at the movie business's recent re-do obsession, featuring an all-star cast of cameos and familiar faces! And I already met with the good folks at Miramax and they're into it, so I'm hoping we'll be shooting in the summer! Never give up, kids. You CAN do anything you want in life, so long as you're patient and malleable."</p>, <p class="body-text"><strong>Want up-to-the-minute entertainment news and features? Just hit 'Like' on our </strong><a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="http://bit.ly/2kxzcFw" href="http://bit.ly/2kxzcFw"><strong><u>Digital Spy Facebook page</u></strong></a><strong> and 'Follow' on our @digitalspy </strong><a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="http://bit.ly/2MED077" href="http://bit.ly/2MED077"><strong><u>Instagram</u></strong></a><strong> and </strong><a class="body-link" data-vars-ga-outbound-link="http://bit.ly/17CUfjS" href="http://bit.ly/17CUfjS"><strong><u>Twitter account</u></strong></a><strong>.</strong></p>]

Pretty soon, he and a tough girl named Maeve are starting an underground therapy clinic for their peers to explore everything they want to know about sex but are too afraid to ask. (If the premise sounds rather implausible, don\u2019t worry: That\u2019s addressed in the video, too.)</p>, <p><span style="color:#333399;"><strong>Press PLAY on the trailer above</strong></span> to begin your\xa0<em>Sex Education</em> \u2014 including hearing Anderson emit the perfect sultry \u201cmrrow\u201d \u2014 then <span style="color:#333399;"><strong>scroll down to see the series\u2019 poster (click on the image to see it in full)</strong></span>. [<p class="article__lede__credit bod-xs m-b-5-xs">Photos by Neilson Barnard via Getty Images and the RSPCA</p>, <p>On December 17, a soulless human <a href="https://news.sky.com/story/dog-tries-to-follow-owner-after-being-abandoned-at-roadside-11591020" target="_blank">dumped</a> a sweet white Staffordshire bull terrier named Snoop on the side of the road in Stoke-on-Trent, England. Footage of this heinous affront to good dogs everywhere was captured on CCTV, released by the <a href="https://www.rspca.org.uk/home" target="_blank">RSPCA</a> around Christmas, and quickly went viral.</p>, <p>The sad saga caught the attention of the OG Snoop, <a href="https://www.vice.com/en_us/article/j5kezx/snoop-dogg-discovers-pine-cone-vgtrn" target="_blank">Snoop Dogg the rapper</a>, who <a href="https://www.dailystar.co.uk/showbiz/750624/snoop-dogg-adopt-abandoned-dog-snoop-rspca-stafford-terrier" target="_blank">offered to adopt</a> the pupper, inviting him to live out his doggy days at \u201cCasa De Snoop.\u201d But distressingly, the RSPCA doesn\u2019t seem interested in Snoop\u2019s generous offer. </p>, <p>A representative <a href="https://people.com/music/snoop-dogg-wants-to-adopt-abandoned-dog-named-snoop/" target="_blank">told PEOPLE</a> that Snoop the dog is currently staying at \u201cprivate kennels\u201d and is not up for adoption while the charity investigates his abandonment, but has had \u201cscores of people wanting to rehome him so we are certain he will not be waiting long for a new home.\u201d</p>, <p>Frankly, this is an affront to the positive energy with which I\u2019d hoped to begin the new calendar year. If a down-on-his-luck dog named Snoop can't be adopted by a wealthy, kind man like Snoop Dogg, what hope is there for the rest of 2019? How will we accumulate enough good karma to expunge the bad memories of 2018, and 2017, and 2016, until we\u2019re back in the good old days when we had a <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2019/01/03/entertainment/obama-billboard-chart-trnd/index.html" target="_blank">president with a sense of humor</a> and spirit of human decency?</p>, <p>Here is an exhaustive list of all the reasons the RSPCA ought to let Snoop Dogg adopt Snoop the dog, becoming the Zaddy Warbucks to his Doggy Orphan Annie:</p>, <p>We, the dog lovers of the internet, can only hope the RSPCA does the right thing and allows two kindred Snoops to become a family. It\u2019d be the ultimate cosmic justice. The wayward soul who dumped Snoop on the side of the road will have ultimately done a good thing by being the impetus for a beautiful canine friendship. </p>, <p><a href="https://confirmsubscription.com/h/i/48178908AA2FD075" target="_blank"><i> Sign up for our newsletter</i></a><i> to get the best of VICE delivered to your inbox daily.</i></p>, <p><i> Follow Kara Weisenstein on </i><a href="https://twitter.com/karaweisenstein" target="_blank"><i> Twitter</i></a><i>.</i></p>, <p class="newsletter__subheading bod-s">Sign up for the best of VICE, delivered to your inbox daily.</p>]
[<p><a href="/user/new">Register</a> - <a href="/forgot-password">Forgot Password</a></p>, <p>By creating an account, you verify that you are at least 13 years of age, and have read and agree to the PopCulture.com <a href="/page/termsofservice">Terms of Service</a> and <a href="/page/privacy">Privacy Policy</a></p>, <p class="author">\n\t\tBy <span>Jose  Bastidas</span>\n<time> - January 3, 2019</time>\n</p>, <p><em>The Blacklist</em>'s upcoming sixth season will change the show that fans know and love, as looming questions will change many of the characters' relationships.</p>, <p>With Elizabeth Keen (Megan Boone) and the audience now aware that Raymond "Red" Reddington (James Spader) isn't who he really is, <a href="//popculture.com/tv-shows/2018/05/17/the-blacklist-ends-with-shocking-revelation/" target="_blank">and Red still unaware that his secret is out</a>, Season 6 will have Liz having the upper hand in her relationship with her "father" for the first time.</p>, <p>"Identity is a big [theme]. It really has been central to the show from the very beginning, but I think now, more than ever, with this reveal that Reddington is, in fact, an impostor and so much of what we've been led to believe has been undermined and eroded," <em>The Blacklist</em> creator Jon Bokenkamp told <a href="//www.etonline.com/the-blacklist-boss-explains-why-season-6-is-a-completely-unique-adventure-exclusive-116446" target="_blank"><em>Entertainment Tonight</em></a> ahead of the beginning of the show's two-night season premiere. "The question at the forefront for the audience and certainly in Elizabeth Keen's mind is: Who is this guy? Why did he choose me? What is his ultimate agenda? Identity is tangled up in that in all kinds of strange, curious ways."</p>, <p>With knowledge on her side, the cat-and-mouse game between Red and Liz will finally see the latter character hiding things and plotting her own agenda during the new installment.</p>, <p>"The thing that is fresh and unique about this season is that for the first time, somebody is way ahead of Red. Elizabeth Keen knows a truth about him that he doesn't know and she is forced to continue to play the role of his daughter," Bokenkamp told the outlet. "In all of the scenes that they play together [this year], not only does he know he is not ultimately the original Raymond Reddington, she also knows that this man is not her father. It creates a really interesting power struggle and a mental chess game between these two characters who are carrying on presenting stories of who they are and yet, Elizabeth Keen is working in the shadows in trying to unlock the truth behind why he entered her life."</p>, <p>The new dynamic will force fans to notice what both Liz and Red say in the silent moments they share during the case of the week episodes.</p>, <p>"That's a dynamic we haven't seen on the show before," Bokenkamp added, saying that it's "something new" creatively for the series. "Elements of it feel familiar but it has consequences that are incredibly significant."</p>, <p>Another big change for the upcoming season, <a href="//popculture.com/tv-shows/2018/12/07/the-blacklist-season-6-trailer-released/" target="_blank">as teased by the Season 6 trailer released in December</a>, will be Red's incarceration. While the development will affect his mysterious master plan, fans can expect to see their favorite criminal mastermind to still thrive despite the new environment.</p>, <p>"He's in prison and all of his superpowers are stripped away," Bokenkamp teased. "His connections, his money means nothing. He's sort of starting over, in a way. That is going to test the relationships he has on the outside and will likely foster some new relationships on the inside. Nobody likes new experiences more than Raymond Reddington, so audiences should expect that he will embrace this new struggle with open arms. It is incredibly dangerous and there are high emotional stakes, but it's also going to be incredibly fun."</p>, <p><em>The Blacklist</em> premieres Season 6 with <a href="//popculture.com/tv-shows/2018/11/22/the-blacklist-season-6-premiere-air-2-nights/" target="_blank">a two-night premiere starting</a> Thursday at 10 p.m. ET, followed by its regular time-slot premiere Friday at 9 p.m. ET on <a href="/category/nbc">NBC</a>.</p>, <p><span class="slidenumber"></span> of <span class="slidetotal"></span></p>, <p>Entertainment Tonight/TV Guide Network. Copyright 2018 PopCulture.com. All rights reserved.</p>]
[<p>\r\n\t\t    The "Follow This Story" feature will notify you when any articles related to this story are posted.\r\n\t\t</p>, <p>\r\n\t\t\tWhen you follow a story, the next time a related article is published \u2014 it could be days, weeks or months \u2014 you'll receive an email informing you of the update.\r\n\t\t</p>, <p>\r\n\t\t\tIf you no longer want to follow a story, click the "Unfollow" link on that story.  There's also an "Unfollow" link in every email notification we send you.\r\n\t\t</p>, <p>\n<span style="color:#900">This tool is available only to subscribers; please make sure you're logged in if you want to follow a story.</span>\n</p>, <p>\n<a href="https://dpw1.pressdemocrat.com/Login.aspx?SentFromUrl=" id="folologin" style="color:#449; float:left">Login</a>\n</p>, <p>\n<span style="color:#900">Please note:</span> This feature is available only to subscribers; make sure you're logged in if you want to follow a story.\r\n\t\t</p>, <p>\n<a href="https://dpw1.pressdemocrat.com/Login.aspx?SentFromUrl=" id="folologin2" style="color:#449; float:left">Login</a><a href="https://dpw1.pressdemocrat.com/Subscribe.aspx" style="color:#449; float:right">Subscribe</a>\n</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">PLAN TO GO?</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">What: Paul Thorn, with Alice Drinks the Kool-Aid</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">When: Fri., Jan. 18, at 8:30 p.m.</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Where: Mystic Theatre, 21 N. Petaluma Blvd.</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Admission: $25</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Tickets: Call (707) 775-6048 or visit MysticTheatre.com.</p>, <p class="first-paragraph">There is a creation story surrounding Paul Thorn, that\u2019s colorful but not entirely true. It goes something like this: Paul Thorn grew up in the Deep South (true) as the son of a strict fire-and-brimstone preacher (true) who forbid his son from playing rock \u2018n roll records (sort of true). So the young Thorn would hide in his bedroom closet and listen to the devil\u2019s music on a small record player (actually, he hid his albums in the closet, but was not prone to spinning platters in the dark, cramped space).</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">\u201cI owned two \u2018satanic\u2019 albums,\u201d Thorn says in a slow Southern murmur, during a phone call from Tupelo, Mississippi, his hometown. \u201cOne was \u201cElton John: Greatest Hits\u201d and the other was Huey Lewis and the News\u2019 first album. </p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">\u201cYou know,\u201d Thorn adds, \u201ctwo of the main demonic message carriers.\u201d</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Thorn\u2019s new album, \u201cDon\u2019t Let the Devil Ride\u201d (Perpetual Obscurity), bristles with his trademark blend of gospel, soul and swampy blues. He digs deeply into such country blues standards as \u201cJesus Gonna Make Up My Dyin\u2019 Bed.\u201d and delivers a rollicking rendition of the old black spiritual \u201cSoon I Will Be Done,\u201d custom-made for a rock \u2019n roll revival meeting. </p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">It\u2019s the perfect mix of the sacred and the profane.</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">\u201cIn the faith that I grew up in, there were two alternatives. You either got saved and went to heaven or you didn\u2019t get saved and you went to hell,\u201d Thorn explains. \u201cLike a lot of religions, they used fear and intimidation, which unfortunately are two things that don\u2019t usually bring success in the long-term. </p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">\u201cThe best way to recruit people,\u201d he adds, \u201cis to love \u2019em.\u201d </p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">His father was a Pentecostal preacher, which did, in a roundabout way, contributd to Thorn becoming an acclaimed blued-eyed soul man steeped in gospel and blues. As a kid, Thorn sang in the church choir. </p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">\u201cThere were two types of churches in Tupelo,\u201d he says. The black churches and the white churches. Our family would attend both churches. That\u2019s where I learned to play music. The black churches had a rhythm-and-blues kind of gospel and the white churches had old-school country spirituals. Those two things made me everything I\u2019ve become - whatever that is.\u201d</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Ask the 54-year-old Thorn to trace his professional career and he offers, \u201cThat\u2019s a very long story.\u201d</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">After high school, he worked in a furniture factory and served in the National Guard. He also fought as a professional boxer, the ninth-ranked middleweight in the country. Thorn once fought WBC middleweight champ Roberto Duran. The fight ended after Thorn received a cut above one of his eyes. The two boxers rode to the hospital in the same ambulance. </p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">\u201cI know that sounds crazy, but it\u2019s the truth,\u201d he says. \u201cDuran had more than I\u2019d ever dealt with before. He was a defensive wizard. He took me to school, man. But I gave a good account of myself. The harsh reality was that at my best, I could never beat him.  But I gave it my all. I left nothing on the table.\u201d</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Thorn\u2019s big break as a musician came when Miles Copeland III - the founder of I.R.S Records, manager of the Police and brother of that band\u2019s drummer, Stewart Copeland - heard a demo cassette tape that Thorn had mailed to him. </p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">PLAN TO GO?</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">What: Paul Thorn, with Alice Drinks the Kool-Aid</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">When: Fri., Jan. 18, at 8:30 p.m.</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Where: Mystic Theatre, 21 N. Petaluma Blvd.</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Admission: $25</p>, <p class="IT-AC_2016-BodyText-BodyText_RR">Tickets: Call (707) 775-6048 or visit MysticTheatre.com.</p>, <p class="first-paragraph-no-border">\u201cLike a lot of wannabe singers, I was just sending out tapes to anybody who would listen,\u201d Thorn says. \u201cMiles Copeland got ahold of one and he liked the songs. At the time, I was playing in a pizza restaurant two nights a week. He literally flew to Tupelo to listen to me playing at a pizza restaurant. A month later, he gave me a bunch of money and I was able to quit the day job at the furniture factory.\u201d</p>, <p>Copeland opened some major doors for Thorn, who soon began touring and building up his fan base. </p>, <p>\u201cIt was just like building a church,\u201d he says. \u201cYou go from city to city and win people over. When you come back around, they bring their friends. You keep doing that over and over. You make relationships, you build friendships and you connect with people.  The church experience really taught me how to draw in people and how to entertain them. Just like my dad did from the pulpit.\u201d </p>, <p>Thorn never did record for I.R.S., but in 1997 he released his debut album, \u201cHammer &amp; Nail,\u201d on the A&amp;M label. The album had nine songs with Biblical themes co-written with legendary Texas songwriter Billy Maddox. It also had one Thorn original (\u201cResurrection Day). </p>, <p>Thorn credits his gospel roots with informing his career as a songwriter.</p>, <p>\u201cYou know, rock \u2019n roll came from gospel,\u201d he says, reflecting on the salvation he\u2019s found in his music. \u201cThere\u2019s no doubt about it, Elvis grew up singing in the same churches I attended in Tupelo. I mean, Led Zeppelin\u2019s music is just a bunch of Mississippi blues songs with distortion. All that came from where I live.\u201d</p>, <p>Thorn\u2019s music is inspirational, as you might expect from a preacher\u2019s son, and they have a clear literary bent.</p>, <p>\u201cA lot of my songs are story songs,\u201d he says. \u201cThere might be something bad going on in the song, but I always try to figure out something in the lyrics that offers the character a way out. I don\u2019t want to wallow in a \u2018we-can\u2019t-get-out-of-this-hole-we\u2019re-in\u2019 scenario. I\u2019m here to say that you can get out of that hole you\u2019re in, because that\u2019s what the message of encouragement is. I\u2019m a secular singer, but I try to put that same hope in my songs that you find in gospel.\u201d</p>, <p>Thorn says believes there is a time and a place for sad songs, and he\u2019s lived his share of sadness.</p>, <p>\u201cBut I\u2019m living something different now,\u201d he says. \u201cI want to be some kind of a light, even if it\u2019s just a small light. I want to be sincere in what I do and to touch people\u2019s hearts.\u201d</p>]

[<p class="entry-meta" data-swiftype-index="false">\n<span class="entry-meta__author">\n<span class="u-lc">by</span>\n<a href="/authors/mike-vulpo">Mike Vulpo</a>\n</span>\n\t\n\t|\n\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t<span class="entry-meta__time">\n\t\t\t\t\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\t\n\t\tThu., Jan. 3, 2019 12:21 PM\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\t\t</span>\n</p>, <p class="image__credits">REX/Shutterstock</p>, <p><strong>Queen Rania of Jordan</strong> is starting a new year on the defense.</p>, <p>After blogs began to share estimated costs of her wardrobe, the 48-year-old royal's office released a rare statement in attempts to set the record straight on her clothes.</p>, <p>"Over the years, there has been a lot of talk about her majesty's spending on clothing," the <a href="https://www.facebook.com/QueenRania/posts/10155743889415826?__xts__[0]=68.ARC4blWzthwkZc5V1mSAMgMYfuRQCYYDcB1XG7XEYC2W4Op-KIOWEalPsYYpH91zMaSgqaDMutsEXYz9gASbqA9LtsXH-cs8odVDAaHfFlVbOUChDtzdUI_yxMj_T8W7BNGqeQDHwIiO6Y5W-gn9c7TqAut5PznVo9uBS0xjY2dNFt6ihHblTJMsX8vfAm1Hl3KzT1Df1l_Xy4ZciQZGZ-nQnso3s_4kpKe7_7RzAQsgj4xYF41u7RRBIIk4G1pJ4rSoJ-iJfdQEqj5LT-ack8ZvOCRoTzJdr0mcZUjRgMQpCi-ExCP2YLvTJVSN72wJXdUHirXD7XQBEQ&amp;__tn__=-R" target="_blank">Facebook</a> post read. "In recognition of Her Majesty's interest in making the facts accessible to all to build their thoughts and opinions on them\u2014positive or negative\u2014we have decided to clarify some details on this subject."</p>, <p>According to the office, Queen Rania of Jordan has always maintained a balance between representing Jordan properly and spending.</p>, <p><strong><a href="https://www.eonline.com/photos/25690/celebs-best-street-style" target="_blank">Celebs' Best Street Style</a></strong></p>, <p>In fact, the majority of her clothing is either loaned or presented as a gift. In other words, it's far different from the "market value" that blog posts tend to focus on.</p>, <p class="image__credits">Dimitrios Kambouris/Getty Images</p>, <p>"The focus on clothing and spending wives of leaders in many countries and accusing them of wastefulness\u2014whether right or wrong\u2014is not new, and has been exploited as a historical political tool. Today, we see some in Jordan adopting this approach to portray Her Majesty the Queen as far from reality, far from the truth," the statement continued. "So they may reject this clarification and question it in principle, in an effort to build a false public opinion."</p>, <p>"We realize that this explanation may be out of the ordinary, but in the absence of facts, rumors and false information are spreading and the wrong impressions accumulate, so we put these details in your hands."</p>, <p>When looking at Queen Rania's Instagram, followers can get a taste of how the royal family member dresses.</p>, <p>Recently, she posed with her family for a holiday card while wearing a sky blue dress. "May we greet the New Year with gratitude for all our blessings and hope for a better tomorrow," she <a href="https://www.instagram.com/p/BriDh8UhgB4/" target="_blank">captioned</a> the picture.</p>, <p>Here's hoping some critics follow her advice.</p>, <p class="rail__text">\n<a class="link--full rail__link" [<p class="article__byline" data-editable="authors">By\n          <span itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">\n<span class="article__author" itemprop="name">\n<a href="/author/amy-nicholson">Amy Nicholson</a></span>\n</span>\n</p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgv9hqn00rl00m3v1etshde@published" data-word-count="31">\n<em>In Slate\u2019s annual Movie Club, film critic Dana Stevens emails with fellow critics\u2014this year, </em><a href="https://www.vanityfair.com/contributor/k-austin-collins"><em>K. Austin Collins</em></a><em>, </em><a href="https://twitter.com/TheAmyNicholson"><em>Amy Nicholson</em></a><em>, and </em><a href="https://twitter.com/BilgeEbiri"><em>Bilge Ebiri</em></a><em>\u2014about the year in cinema. </em><a href="https://slate.com/culture/2019/01/thanos-avatar-2018-movies.html"><em>Read the first entry here.</em></a><em> </em>\n</p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvao8c00103g5vortwrgpd@published" data-word-count="4">\n          All hail the queen.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoti001j3g5vhgg1v87k@published" data-word-count="35">\n          I\u2019m happy to gush about <strong><em>The Favourite</em></strong>, though <a href="https://slate.com/culture/2019/01/death-stalin-iannucci-best-political-comedy-slate-movie-club.html">that barbecue sauce</a> has gotta stay on Dana\u2019s chin, in deference to Olivia Colman\u2019s Queen Anne doing an entire scene with her face smeared in cake vomit.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaodh00143g5veu22tm8i@published" data-word-count="85">\n          Yorgos Lanthimos is exactly my tempo, down to the sharp violins he uses as drums. I love his cynicism, his clipped sentences, his ability to see the strings that propel human behavior as clearly as if we were marionettes. Yet, I can\u2019t argue with people who\u2019ve grumbled that he wants his actors wooden\u2014he\u2019s the one guy who doesn\u2019t allow Colin Farrell to wiggle his eyebrows. Personally, I get a kick out of Lanthimos\u2019 Noh-style performances, which force us to pay more attention to the dialogue.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoax00113g5vzgq07ith@published" data-word-count="60">\n          But in<em> The Favourite</em>, Lanthimos lets Colman bloom as a vulnerable, maddening queen whose moods change as fast as we can read them. No wonder Emma Stone and Rachel Weisz, the two courtiers vying for her attention, can\u2019t win. They can only destroy each other, and our empathy for them, which seesaws back and forth as their statuses get wobblier.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaobq00123g5v8tuoff24@published" data-word-count="92">\n          In a Lanthimos society, the characters who behave perfectly are the most ridiculous. Our rituals themselves are bunk. He\u2019s got plenty to mock in Queen Anne\u2019s court\u2014that slo-mo duck race!\u2014but he\u2019s most interested in questioning the best way to be loved. Stone\u2019s Abigail, a scullery maid whose big blue eyes have seen a lot of misery, lavishes the queen with praise. Weisz\u2019s Lady Sarah is brutal. When the queen looks like a badger, she tells her. One loves how we want to be loved; the other delivers the love we might need.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaodc00133g5v39p7bp2n@published" data-word-count="91">\n          Lanthimos tricks us into rooting for Abigail only to about-face and side with Lady Sarah. False kindness is worse than cruel honesty. And now that Lanthimos himself is poised to be hailed as one of this generation\u2019s greatest filmmakers, I wonder if he\u2019s uncertain about that crown.<br/>Perhaps the provocateur fears that audiences will start to unquestioningly agree that he\u2019s a genius. I suspect he needs his films to put up a fight. Colman\u2019s puke-plastered Queen Anne earns our affection by being stubbornly, frustratingly, repulsively herself. He wants to do the same.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaodn00153g5vet5xpmuc@published" data-word-count="117">\n          Speaking of foreign rulers, I spent a fair chunk of this year at international film festivals, many of which have a more complex relationship with their government than, say, the Toronto International Film Festival. My most far-flung trip was to the Eurasia International Film Festival in Kazakhstan, which was recently strong-armed into switching locations from the cultural center of Almaty, an ancient city on the Silk Road, to the country\u2019s new capital, Astana, a once-empty wasteland now populated with futuristic skyscrapers, some designed by President Nursultan Nazarbayev himself. Literally\u2014there\u2019s a video of him sketching the Bayterek Tower, a 300-foot-tall structure featuring a golden egg where, at the top, visitors can touch his handprint. (It, too, is gold.)\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoek00163g5vlrl2ht3j@published" data-word-count="58">\n          The decision to trade Almaty for Astana is like if Sundance relocated to Mar-a-Lago. Not that I\u2019m complaining that some festival screenings were inside a yurt-shaped mall with rollercoasters and an indoor beach with real sand. Real sand! I buried my toes in it and drank three mojitos to soothe the headache of watching Azerbaijan\u2019s first horror flick.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaofp00173g5vgh8ga0m1@published" data-word-count="80">\n          Everything is politics, even Eurasia\u2019s opening night party, headed by Serbian director Emir Kusturica and the No Smoking Orchestra. Maybe you know Kusturica from winning the Palme d\u2019Or, twice. Maybe you know him from <a href="https://www.nbcnews.com/news/world/guess-who-came-dinner-flynn-putin-n742696">that infamous picture in Moscow</a> where he shared a dinner table with Vladimir Putin, Michael Flynn, and Jill Stein. Maybe you have a good theory about why he was rocking out in a huge sombrero and Zapata bandoliers? I just threw up my hands and danced.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaogc00183g5vvwbmunyo@published" data-word-count="46">\n          There are two questions you ponder when you go to a lot of international film festivals. One: Why does every opening night hire a faux Charlie Chaplin? Two: What can we learn about the world from the stories their filmmakers tell, and how they tell them?\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoh700193g5vhleo1co3@published" data-word-count="114">\n          Bilge has much more authority on the topic than I do, but <a href="https://www.indiewire.com/2018/04/istanbul-film-festival-turkey-censorship-1201957551/">in Istanbul</a>, I had long, wine-soaked talks with Turkish artists about what\u2019s changed in the three years since the government began enforcing a registration certificate law that functions like censorship. Political films that displease the minister of culture can\u2019t get a stamp. Without a stamp, they can\u2019t be shown\u2014not even at the festival, which had a tense standoff in 2015 over a documentary that humanized the Kurdistan guerrillas. At the last minute, the ministry canceled the screening. In response, two dozen directors canceled their own screenings, the jury refused to judge, the closing ceremony was called off, and the festival director quit.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoip001a3g5v8ufvk3yy@published" data-word-count="72">\n          This year was calmer, but what struck me about the films that squeaked through was that many of them, too, were political\u2014they\u2019d just hidden their anxieties, in time-honored fashion, in science fiction and absurdism. They told stories about towns being emptied because of an unknown stench, of immortal women who live to see every person in their life disappear, of Brechtian truth-tellers attacked for trying to keep their bosses honest.<br/>Everything <em>is</em> politics.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoj5001b3g5vl7im7ker@published" data-word-count="184">\n          At the Cairo International Film Festival, things appeared to be more liberal. One of the hot tickets was a local male director\u2019s take on abortion, a confrontational film that boasted close-ups of a fetus in a Ziploc bag and a dead giraffe. I vastly preferred Meryem Benm\u2019Barek\u2019s <strong><em>Sofia</em></strong>, an agitprop drama about a single, pregnant girl who\u2019s less scared of motherhood than of Morocco\u2019s criminalization of unmarried sex. I don\u2019t want to give away the ending, but let me just say there are even worse punishments than jail. On that topic: At our awards show, an Egyptian actress named Rania Youssef wore a dress with a see-through gauze skirt. The next day, <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/12/02/world/middleeast/egypt-rania-youssef-dress.html">she was arrested for public obscenity</a> and faced up to five years in prison. <a href="https://en.vogue.me/fashion/news/charges-dropped-egyptian-actress-rania-youssef-revealing-dress/">Charges were dropped</a> after Youssef begged for forgiveness. (Other female Egyptian celebs haven\u2019t been so lucky, like the pop star\xa0<a href="https://www.timesofisrael.com/egyptian-pop-star-sentenced-to-2-years-for-racy-banana-eating-video/">sentenced to two years in jail</a>\xa0for suggestively eating a banana.) Going forward, all actresses on the festival\u2019s red carpet must adhere to a dress code, with Egypt\u2019s actor\u2019s union volunteering to discipline any woman who shows too much skin.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaopu001c3g5vr9zlsi31@published" data-word-count="58">\n          The best foreign language film I saw this year was <strong><em>Suleiman Mountain</em></strong>, a black dramedy about a con man and his two wives scamming their way across Kyrgyzstan in an East German camper. <em>Suleiman Mountain</em> has not gotten a real release in the states, but until it does, imagine <em>Shoplifters</em> on the road with a dash more bitters.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaopz001d3g5vimtzd6zn@published" data-word-count="91">\n          Boy, has it been a fantastic year for international cinema. <strong><em>Burning</em></strong> is terrific, though I agree with Kam that I\u2019d have traded the whole third act for five more minutes of Jong-seo Jeon\u2019s pantomimes. And <strong><em>Shoplifters</em></strong> knocked me sideways. I\u2019ll admit, I clench up when a film threatens Uncannily Wise Children, but Hirokazu Kore-eda stripped away my reservations like I was a convenience store with lousy security. I\u2019ll see <em>Roma</em>\u2019s beach scene and raise it the image of this hodgepodge family holding hands in the surf as their <em>obaasan</em> watches on.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoq1001e3g5vi8495hly@published" data-word-count="148">\n          My favorite foreign festival, by the way, was the series of documentary shorts I saw at the <a href="https://www.pbs.org/newshour/world/its-been-such-a-long-time-since-ive-seen-a-flower-life-in-a-syrian-refugee-camp">Azraq refugee camp in Jordan</a>, made by Syrian teenagers who\u2019d spent the past three years living in small boxes with their entire families. I was there with a dozen volunteers from Epic Magazine to help guide the kids in making their own movies. My group, five boys between 17 and 20, had a stack of still photographs that they wanted to use to make something experimental, too, though they didn\u2019t have the vocabulary\u2014or really, the film library\u2014to put their ambition into words. Someone smarter than me showed them their first clips of <em>Gates of Heaven</em> and <em>La Jet\xe9e</em>, and a lightbulb flicked on in their imagination. In a year of great movie moments from around the globe, that memory best proves the power of cinema to inspire people, wherever they are.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoq4001f3g5vt4invp89@published" data-word-count="16">\n          What\u2019s that moment for you, Bilge? It\u2019s a big question, but you\u2019ve got a big brain.\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph slate-paragraph--tombstone" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoq7001g3g5vq1v60t4v@published" data-word-count="1">\n          xo,<br/>A\n        </p>, <p class="slate-paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="slate.com/_components/slate-paragraph/instances/cjqgvaoq9001i3g5v2hi0w4cm@published" data-word-count="4">\n<em><a href="https://slate.com/culture/2019/01/first-reformed-ethan-hawke-performance-slate-movie-club.html">Read the previous entry.</a></em>\n</p>, <p>\n            Slate is published by The Slate Group, a Graham Holdings Company.<br/>\n            All contents \xa9 2019 The Slate Group LLC. [<p>Scottish actor, comedian, and musician Billy Connolly has led a remarkable career, one that\u2019s found him opening for Elton John, lending his voice to multiple Disney movies, Hobbiting with Peter Jackson, and laying waste in the <em>Boondock Saints</em> franchise. Now, the man who has brought no shortage of laughter to the world is culling tears. In an upcoming BBC Scotland documentary series on his life and career, Connolly speaks candidly about his struggle with Parkinson\u2019s disease and the knowledge that his life is \u201cslipping away\u201d from him.</p>, <p>\u201cMy life is slipping away and I can feel it, and I should, I\u2019m 75,\u201d he says in the documentary. \u201cI\u2019m near the end but it doesn\u2019t frighten me. It\u2019s an adventure, and it\u2019s quite interesting to see myself slipping away. Bits slip off and leave me. Talents leave and attributes leave. I don\u2019t have the balance I used to have; I don\u2019t have the energy I used to have; I can\u2019t hear the way I used to hear; I can\u2019t see as good as I used to. I can\u2019t remember the way I used to remember.\u201d <br/></p>, <p class="ad-label proxima"><small class="proxima">Advertisement</small></p>, <p class="ad-label-bottom"></p>, <p>He also remarks\xa0on how his condition is impacting his music, a part of his career that\u2019s been with him since he worked the Glasgow shipyards as a young man. \u201cI can\u2019t work my left hand on the banjo. It\u2019s as if I\u2019m being prepared for something, some other adventure which is over the hill. I\u2019ve got all this stuff to lose first, and then I\u2019ll be on the shadowy side of the hill, doing the next episode in the spirit world.\u201d</p>, <p>He also acknowledges that \u201cit\u2019s going to get worse,\u201d but not without embracing a bit of hope. \u201cThere\u2019s still time to go yet,\u201d he adds. \u201cThere\u2019s still places to go, new friends to make, maybe new songs to write and sing and jokes to tell,\u201d he says. We sure hope so. </p>, <p><em>Billy Connolly: Made in Scotland</em> will air on BBC2 this Friday evening. Bring tissues. </p>, <p class="ad-label proxima"><small class="proxima">Advertisement</small></p>, <p class="ad-label-bottom"></p>, <p>[<a href="https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/billy-connolly-i-feel-myself-slipping-away-tccpm092l" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/billy-connolly-i-feel-myself-slipping-away-tccpm092l', {metric25:1})" rel="noopener" target="_blank">via <em>The Times</em></a>]</p>, <p class="author-bio__bio">Randall Colburn is a Chicago-based writer and occasional playwright. He is a senior writer at Consequence of Sound and a talking head in Best Worst Movie, the documentary about Troll 2.</p>]
[<p data-page="1">If you want to stay at the <a href="https://hardrockhotel.com/" target="_blank">Hard Rock Hotel &amp; Casino</a> in Las Vegas, you'd better grab a room before fall. The storied site will close for about four months before it re-emerges as a <a href="https://virginhotels.com/" target="_blank">Virgin Hotel</a> in 2020.</p>, <p>Dates are still fuzzy on exactly when all of this will take place at the resort two miles east of the Strip at Harmon Avenue and Paradise Road.</p>, <p>\u201cYou\u2019ve got one opportunity to really enter the market,\u201d said Richard Bosworth, chief executive of JC Hospitality, which owns the property. \u201cAnd we want to make sure that we\u2019re doing that correctly and that we\u2019re not piecemealing aspects of the property: a restaurant here, a hotel room there.\u201d</p>, <p>Bosworth said keeping the hotel open during the transition would have been too disruptive for guests.</p>, <p>Virgin Hotels currently operates hotels in San Francisco and Chicago, with more planned. Renovated rooms will look like other Virgin hotels, with a design that\u2019s \u201cmodern, contemporary, light and airy, authentic [and] welcoming,\u201d Raul Leal, chief executive of Virgin Hotels, said.</p>, <p>The hotel\u2019s popular music venue, <a href="https://hardrockhotel.com/las-vegas-entertainment/1-joint-overview.php" target="_blank">the Joint</a>, will remain, but also will be upgraded and maybe renamed. Rehab, the Hard Rock\u2019s five-acre party pool area, closed last October and will be redeveloped prior to the 2020 reopening.</p>, <p>No decisions have yet been made about which restaurants and bars the new Virgin Hotel will partner with. \u201cWhen we open it, we want people to go, \u2018Oh, wow\u2019 [with] one big grand opening,\u201d Leal said.</p>, <p>The new Virgin site will compete with the city\u2019s trendier hotels \u2014 <a href="https://www.cosmopolitanlasvegas.com/" target="_blank">the Cosmopolitan of Las Vegas</a>, <a href="http://www.delanolasvegas.com/en.html" target="_blank">Delano</a> and recently opened <a href="https://www.nomadlasvegas.com/en.html" target="_blank">NoMad</a>.</p>, <p>\u201cAll those do properties do a great job \u2026 but have their own identities,\u201d Leal said.</p>, <p>The Hard Rock opened in 1995 and has 1,504 rooms. The 80-foot-tall guitar that greeted arriving guests for more than two decades was dismantled in September 2017.</p>, <p>Even though the Hard Rock will shutter later this year, Bosworth is hoping to keep <a href="https://magicmikelivelasvegas.com/" target="_blank">\u201cMagic Mike Live,\u201d</a> a male revue, running during the closure. He confirmed that co-producer Channing Tatum and others are scouting a new home and that the show would be a good fit for the Virgin portfolio.</p>, <p>Vegas won\u2019t be without the Hard Rock name, however. The <a href="https://www.hardrock.com/cafes/las-vegas/" target="_blank">Hard Rock Cafe Las Vegas</a>, unrelated to the hotel, stands at a separate location at 3771 S. Las Vegas Blvd.</p>]

[<p><a href="https://news.avclub.com/johnny-depps-rotting-spirit-has-finally-been-exorcised-1831262096" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'Internal link', 'https://news.avclub.com/johnny-depps-rotting-spirit-has-finally-been-exorcised-1831262096', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow">In December</a>, Disney quietly indicated that the next <em>Pirates Of The Caribbean </em>movie would not feature series star Johnny Depp, with <em>Deadpool </em>writing team Rhett Reese and Paul Wernick coming on board to the give the unnecessarily long-running series \u201ca kick in the pants.\u201d The most recent film in the series, 2017's <a href="https://film.avclub.com/pirates-of-the-caribbean-slogs-out-to-sea-for-the-fifth-1798191423" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'Internal link', 'https://film.avclub.com/pirates-of-the-caribbean-slogs-out-to-sea-for-the-fifth-1798191423', {metric25:1})" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><em>Dead Men Tell No Tales</em></a>, made a shitload of money worldwide but set a new low bar for the series in the states, which is a problem when a movie costs $230 million to make. Unsurprisingly a good chunk of that money went straight into Johnny Depp\u2019s gross, sequined pockets, and <a href="https://www.forbes.com/sites/guymartin/2018/12/31/how-to-save-a-fast-90-million-on-your-pirates-movie-write-johnny-depp-out-of-the-thing/#4957d8441cda" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'https://www.forbes.com/sites/guymartin/2018/12/31/how-to-save-a-fast-90-million-on-your-pirates-movie-write-johnny-depp-out-of-the-thing/#4957d8441cda', {metric25:1})" rel="noopener" target="_blank">according to <em>Forbes</em></a>, Disney will save a reported $90 million just by leaving Depp back on the shore for the next movie (since that\u2019s apparently his per-<em>Pirate</em> fee).</p>, <p><em>Forbes </em>seems to be concerned that this is a bad idea, as Depp can still \u201crake in the lucre\u201d (<a href="https://news.avclub.com/johnny-depp-is-hollywood-s-most-overpaid-actor-again-1798255102" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'Internal link', 'https://news.avclub.com/johnny-depp-is-hollywood-s-most-overpaid-actor-again-1798255102', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow">which is arguable</a>), but the larger issue with Depp is something that <em>Forbes </em>glosses over as \u201csome personal problems\u201d that have\u2014hopefully\u2014made him a bit toxic in Hollywood. Today, <a href="https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/thr-esq/johnny-depp-amber-heard-legal-documents-shed-new-light-dual-abuse-accounts-1171081?utm_source=twitter" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/thr-esq/johnny-depp-amber-heard-legal-documents-shed-new-light-dual-abuse-accounts-1171081?utm_source=twitter', {metric25:1})" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><em>The Hollywood Reporter </em>has published a story</a> on some court documents it has obtained regarding allegations that Depp abused ex-wife Amber Heard, including this quote from Heard that she gave during a deposition: \u201cJohnny and I refer to his other personality, the part of him that is present when he beats me up\u2014we call that the monster and have called [that] the monster for many years.\u201d</p>, <p class="ad-label proxima"><small class="proxima">Advertisement</small></p>, <p class="ad-label-bottom"></p>, <p>In the documents, Heard also describes one night in 2016 where Depp allegedly threw a phone at Heard\u2019s head \u201cas hard as he could.\u201d A neighbor responded to Heard calling for help and said in court that she saw Depp swinging around a bottle of wine and smashing things with it. Heard didn\u2019t file a police report, saying her lawyers had advised against it, and Depp described the situation completely differently in his own statements, saying that he had gently tossed the phone in question onto a couch and that it was actually Heard who injured herself by smashing things. The divorce was finalized in 2016, with Heard donating her<a href="https://news.avclub.com/amber-heard-donates-her-entire-7-million-divorce-settl-1798250826" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'Internal link', 'https://news.avclub.com/amber-heard-donates-her-entire-7-million-divorce-settl-1798250826', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow"> entire $7 million settlement to charity </a>and both sides<a href="https://news.avclub.com/johnny-depp-and-amber-heard-settle-domestic-violence-ca-1798250698" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'Internal link', 'https://news.avclub.com/johnny-depp-and-amber-heard-settle-domestic-violence-ca-1798250698', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow"> releasing a joint statement</a> that essentially said nobody made \u201cfalse accusations\u201d and that neither of them ever intended to physically abuse the other.</p>, <p>So, by leaving Depp out of the next <em>Pirates </em>movie, Disney can avoid being associated with all of that <em>and </em>avoid paying him $90 million\u2014a deal that the team behind <em>The Crimes Of Grindelwald </em><a href="https://www.avclub.com/fantastic-beasts-2-director-defends-casting-alleged-abu-1820817763" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'Internal link', 'https://www.avclub.com/fantastic-beasts-2-director-defends-casting-alleged-abu-1820817763', {metric25:1})" rel="noopener" target="_blank">apparently didn\u2019t consider</a>. </p>]
