[<p>Idea for a new episode of HBO\u2019s <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curb_Your_Enthusiasm" rel="noopener" target="_blank">\u201cCurb Your Enthusiasm.\u201d</a></p>, <p>Marty Funkhouser has died. Larry, Cheryl, Jeff, and Susie are heartbroken at the death of their friend, and they make a shiva call. Larry and Cheryl have brought a box of rugelach for the shiva table. Throughout the shiva call, Larry watches the shiva table, and sees that no one is eating the rugelach.</p>, <p>Angry at having brought the rugelach (after all, the bakery was in Beverly Hills, quite a distance from his usual hood in Santa Monica), Larry steals the rugelach at the end of the shiva call by hiding it in his shirt.</p>, <p>On the way to his car, Larry runs into the rabbi, who tells him that anyone who takes food from a shiva home is in danger of being cursed. The rest of the episode is filled with typical Larry David mishaps. At the end of the episode, he leaves the box of rugelach on the steps of the shiva house and drives away, believing himself to be free of the curse.</p>, <p>At which point, he drives his car into the rabbi\u2019s car, and the theme music comes on.</p>, <p>I know what you\u2019re saying.</p>, <p>\u201cDon\u2019t quit your day job!\u201d</p>, <p>I felt an instant twinge of sadness in learning of the <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/02/obituaries/bob-einstein-dead.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">death</a> of actor Bob Einstein at the age of 76. Bob had a plethora of screen and television roles, but the one that I will remember the most, and the reason that I mourn him, is for his role of Marty Funkhouser on \u201cCurb Your Enthusiasm.\u201d</p>, <p>Why?</p>, <p>Television certainly has no shortage of Jewish characters.</p>, <p>But, \u201cCurb\u201d was uniquely Jewish.</p>, <p>Almost every character was Jewish \u2014 <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_David" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Larry David;\xa0</a>his manager, Jeff Greene (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeff_Garlin" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Jeff Garlin</a>) and his wife, Susie (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Susie_Essman" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Susie Essman</a>); Larry\u2019s father, played by the late <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shelley_Berman" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Shelley Berman</a>; and comedian <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Lewis_(comedian)" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Richard Lewis</a>, playing himself. There were exceptions, as well \u2014 especially Larry\u2019s wife, Cheryl (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheryl_Hines" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Cheryl Hines).</a></p>, <p>Moreover, \u201cCurb\u201d had so many Jewish plot lines that the series practically constitutes an anthology of Jewish short fiction.</p>, <p>Among my favorites:</p>, <p>And yet, of all the Jewish characters, the one that stands out in my mind was <a href="https://www.tvovermind.com/top-five-marty-funkhouser-moments-curb-enthusiasm/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Marty Funkhouser</a>, played by Bob Einstein, of blessed memory.</p>, <p>Here is why.</p>, <p>While \u201cCurb\u201d is filled with Jewish characters (and the actors that play them), most of them are somewhat inactive Jews.</p>, <p>True \u2014 in one episode, Larry gets in trouble for scalping High Holy Day tickets in synagogue, which turns out to be a biting satire of the oft-discussed practice.</p>, <p>But, in most cases and in most situations, and for most of the characters, Jewish identity is unremarkable.</p>, <p>Except for Marty Funkhouser.</p>, <p>First, Marty is a mensch \u2014 perhaps the only true mensch in the series. He is the proud, supportive father of a transgender man.</p>, <p>Moreover, Marty makes no excuses for his Judaism. He embraces it. When his father died, Marty sat a traditional shiva. He grew as a Jew. He started wearing a kippah. In \u201cPalestinian Chicken,\u201d he deliberately wore the kippah to the Palestinian restaurant \u2014\xa0 because he wanted to proudly trumpet his Jewish identity, even in \u201cenemy\u201d territory.</p>, <p>Yes, \u201cCurb\u201d is a comedy. And, yes, Marty could be a little insufferable and a tad self-righteous at times.</p>, <p>But, as a Jewish character, he might have been the most affirmatively Jewish character in recent television history.</p>, <p>Bob Einstein was a great actor, and by all reports, a sweet, kind man.</p>, <p>May his family find the comfort they deserve. And may he make God laugh.</p>, <p>\xa0</p>, <p>Rabbi Jeffrey K. Salkin is the spiritual leader of Temple Solel in Hollywood, Fla., and the author of numerous books on Jewish spirituality and ethics, published by Jewish Lights Publishing and Jewish Publication Society.</p>]

[<p>Back in December 2017, Motherboard highlighted the work of a Redditor called deepfakes who was creating these videos, which can appear quite realistic. They\u2019ve since been banned by the likes of <a href="https://www.techspot.com/news/72981-discord-shuts-down-group-shared-ai-edited-fake.html">Discord</a>, Twitter, and GIF-hosting platform Gfycat. Pornhub was supposed to have <a href="https://www.techspot.com/news/73154-pornhub-bans-non-consensual-ai-edited-fake-porn.html">done the same thing</a>, but they're still easily found on site. Moreover, they\u2019ve now become more realistic while the software behind them is easier to use.</p>, <p>Speaking to the <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2018/12/31/scarlett-johansson-fake-ai-generated-sex-videos-nothing-can-stop-someone-cutting-pasting-my-image/?noredirect=on&amp;utm_term=.9c3ee58a2dcb">Washington Post</a>, Johansson, who is Hollywood\u2019s highest-paid actress, spoke out about the practice. The Avengers star appears in many of the videos, including one that has been viewed over 1.5 million times.</p>, <p>\u201cNothing can stop someone from cutting and pasting my image or anyone else\u2019s onto a different body and making it look as eerily realistic as desired,\u201d she said. \u201cThe fact is that trying to protect yourself from the Internet and its depravity is basically a lost cause [...] The Internet is a vast wormhole of darkness that eats itself.\u201d</p>, <p>While most deepfake clips use images of stars such as Maisie Williams, Taylor Swift, Aubrey Plaza, and Gal Gadot, not every victim is a celebrity. A <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2018/12/30/fake-porn-videos-are-being-weaponized-harass-humiliate-women-everybody-is-potential-target">Washington Post</a> story highlighted a woman in her 40s who\u2019s likeness appears in a video, though it\u2019s unclear why she was targeted.</p>, <p>While forensic tools have been <a href="https://www.techspot.com/news/75893-defense-department-has-produced-first-tools-catching-deepfakes.html">developed</a> by the Defense Department for catching deepfake videos and fake news created using the same techniques, it's still a legal grey area. Unlike <a href="https://www.techspot.com/news/66843-celebgate-hacker-sentenced-18-months-federal-prison.html">The Fappening</a>, which saw explicit photos of celebs including Johansson posted online, no personal data is stolen when creating the clips. Johansson also noted that different countries have different copyright laws, further complicating the matter.</p>, <p>\xa9 2019 TechSpot, Inc. [<p><em>90 Day Fiance</em> star Ashley Martson is FINALLY clearing up all the confusion about why she and husband Jay Smith had three different weddings, including one in Jamaica, one in Las Vegas, and the other in Pennsylvania.</p>, <p>To get you all caught up, there were <a href="https://starcasm.net/90-day-fiance-jay-ashley-wedding-photos-leak-jamaica/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">photos leaked in early December</a> of what appeared to be Ashley and Jay\u2019s formal wedding ceremony in Jamaica. Jay would later explain that this was a commitment ceremony from 2017 so that his friends and family in Jamaica could attend.</p>, <p>Then, on the show, we see Ashley and Jay getting married in Las Vegas in a kitschy Elvis-themed ceremony. However, we could find no record of Jay and Ashley getting married in or near Las Vegas. Plus, Ashley\u2019s (former?) best friend Natalie later shared photos of herself in Las Vegas for the wedding, and she stated on Instagram that Ashley and Jay were already married. (<a href="https://starcasm.net/90-day-fiance-jay-ashley-still-together-fake/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">You can click here for a full recap of all the fishiness surrounding Ashleyy and Jay\u2019s story line this season.</a>)</p>, <p>OK Ashley, take it away\u2026</p>, <p>\u201cI know there are some rumors,\u201d Ashley began an Instagram post from moments ago, \u201cso I spoke with TLC they would like me to clarify: We scheduled our original wedding on the 88th day after Jay arrived to America. Due to canceling our original wedding plans so last minute (as you saw on the show during the wedding registry incident) and having my kids that weekend, we could not go to Vegas before the 90 days were up. Jay and I went to City Hall in Harrisburg, PA, said our vows, then flew out to Vegas for an actual ceremony a week later.\u201d</p>, <p>She continues: \u201cThis is why no one can find a public certificate in the Vegas records. Boy</em>:</strong> \u201c<em>Beautiful Boy</em> [which is about a father and his son, who is addicted to drugs] was a script they\u2019d been trying to get made for 10 years. Every guy actor my age had gone up for it. I\u2019ve been lucky, but a lot of the bigger Hollywood movies like <em>Spider-Man</em>, things like that, I didn\u2019t get. So, for <em>Beautiful Boy</em>, I did a lot of research and read about drugs, and I brought the books to my first meeting with the director. I could see in his eyes that he was thinking, This kid is nuts. But I felt this movie\u2014the subject of drug addiction\u2014was so important. I wanted to make an anti-glorification-of-drugs movie. And I think we did.\u201d</p>, <p><strong>On meeting Nic Sheff, who he plays in the film:</strong> \u201cYes. I met him a week before we started shooting. And there was nothing about Nic that fit my stereotype of an addict. That was the learning grace of this movie: Nic is alive and well, but the reality is, it\u2019s a day at a time. You never really beat it.\u201d</p>, <p><strong>On losing weight for the role:</strong> \u201cMy mom was worried! I lost 18 pounds. First, I\u2019m in a movie where I was having sex with a peach, and then it was like, \u2018I got another movie!\u2019 She said, \u2018Great!\u2019 And then I had to tell her what it was about.\u201d</p>, <p>For more from <strong>Timothee</strong>, visit <a class="external" href="https://www.wmagazine.com/gallery/best-performances-nicole-kidman-claire-foy-rami-malek" onclick="ga('send', 'event', 'Outgoing Links', '/outgoing/https://www.wmagazine.com/gallery/best-performances-nicole-kidman-claire-foy-rami-malek')" rel="external" target="_blank">WMagazine.com</a>.</p>, <p>Follow Just Jared Jr. on Twitter!</p>, <p>Become a Fan on Facebook!</p>]

According to a new-year report from data, music consumption company BuzzAngle, Latin music consumption is now more popular than that of country music.</p>, <p>According to the report, Latin music accounted for 9.4 percent of all album listening in the United States in 2018. It was reportedly measured by combining the physical and digital sales, song downloads, and on-demand streams. The growth in music consumption surpassed country music consumption, which only accounted for 8.7 percent of all album consumption in the U.S.</p>, <p>The prior year, country music accounted for 8.1 percent of album-listening, while Latin music clocked in at 7.5 percent.</p>, <p>Individual song-listening has also increased in popularity. In the past year, fans have increased their consumption from 9.5 percent to 10.8 percent. Country music is still behind at 7.8 percent. Latin artist video views have also increased to 24.3 percent from 21.9 percent.</p>, <p>While country music still dominates on the radio, the Latin music genre is reportedly closing in on R&amp;B and rock, which are tallied at 11.2 percent and 11.7 percent respectively.</p>, <p>The music industry better look out because Latin music is bound to keep climbing the ladder in the new year.</p>, <p>Rae Sremmurd's Slim Jxmmi was reportedly involved in a street brawl in New Zealand on Thursday (Jan. 3) that ended with one person being stabbed, TMZ reports.</p>, <p>The incident reportedly occurred while Slim Jxmmi was walking through the streets of New Zealand's downtown Auckland. Footage obtained by the celebrity site shows the 26-year-old getting physical with several other people as a man \u2013 who is believe to be the rapper's bodyguard \u2013 throws punches in his defense.</p>, <p>The altercation allegedly ensued after someone allegedly attempted to record Slim Jxmmi and friends while they were walking. Witnesses on the scene alleged they saw a broken bottle being used as a weapon, which may have ultimately led to the stabbing. One individual was reportedly taken to the Auckland City Hospital to be treated for stab wounds.</p>, <p>Rae Sremmurd's other member, Swae Lee, was not present at the time. While neither the video nor witnesses have indicated that Slim Jxmmi committed the stabbing, it's unclear if local law enforcement are investigating him at this time.</p>, <p>Rae Sremmurd is currently visiting New Zealand and Australia as part of a handful of tour dates.</p>, <p>Check out the footage of the violent altercation in the video above.</p>, <p>A $100,000 reward is now available for anyone who has credible information, which will lead to the arrest of the white man who shot and killed 7-year-old Jazmine Barnes.</p>, <p>"We want to make sure that we get the right person as quickly as possible,"\xa0Sheriff Ed Gonzalez said during a press conference.</p>, <p>The unprovoked attack sent shockwaves through the\xa0Harris County community, leaving many\xa0wanting justice for Jazmine and her surviving family members. Police are hoping the sketched description offered by Jazmine's sisters will help capture the killer.\xa0Until then, all law enforcement have to work with is a\xa0grainy\xa0image of the getaway vehicle, a red extended cab pick-up truck.</p>, <p>Along with the reward money, a Go Fund Me account has been established to assist with Jazmine's funeral. [<p class="article-paragraph" data-reactid="109"><!-- react-text: 110 -->It's day two of 2019, but <!-- /react-text --><a data-reactid="111" href="https://www.wmagazine.com/topic/lady-gaga">Lady Gaga</a><!-- react-text: 112 --> is well on her way to having her best year ever. The face of <!-- /react-text --><em data-reactid="113">A Star Is Born</em><!-- react-text: 114 --> is not only poised to dominate the cultural conversation around the <!-- /react-text --><a data-reactid="115" href="https://www.wmagazine.com/story/golden-globes-2019-nominations">upcoming awards season</a><!-- react-text: 116 --> and already inspired countless headlines about her <!-- /react-text --><a data-reactid="117" href="https://www.wmagazine.com/story/lady-gaga-enigma-las-vegas-show">Las Vegas residency</a><!-- react-text: 118 -->, which just kicked off; she's also getting ready to launch her career in the beauty world. The website for her upcoming beauty line Haus Beauty has already done as much, with the domain <!-- /react-text --><a data-reactid="119" href="https://www.hausbeauty.com/">now live</a><!-- react-text: 120 --> and directing users to enter their email address for updates.<!-- /react-text --></p>, <p class="article-paragraph" data-reactid="121"><!-- react-text: 122 -->Here's what we know about Haus Beauty: Gaga originally filed to trademark the name, a reference to her creative team Haus of Gaga, back in May. At the time, the pop star's company Ate My Heart Inc. made the move, as reported by <!-- /react-text --><a data-reactid="123" href="https://theblast.com/lady-gaga-trademark-haus-beauty/">The Blast</a><!-- react-text: 124 -->. Then, at least five days ago, one of Gaga's many devoted fans noticed that a website for Haus Beauty had gone live.<!-- /react-text --></p>, <p class="instagram-media-more" data-reactid="131"><a data-reactid="132" href="https://www.instagram.com/p/Br6iF3Ngt7R/" target="blank">View on Instagram</a></p>, <p class="article-paragraph" data-reactid="133"><!-- react-text: 134 -->It's not at all surprising that Gaga would pivot to commodifying her unique approach to beauty\u2014after all, she already has a perfume brand named after her 2009 debut album <!-- /react-text --><em data-reactid="135">The Fame</em><!-- react-text: 136 -->. She also has firsthand experience in the beauty world as a campaign star for M.A.C. Viva Glam in 2009 and 2011. As with much of her career, Gaga has seized on good timing. Because she's more of a household name than ever before, thanks largely to her role in one of the year's most talked-about films, it makes perfect sense that Gaga would now unleash her beauty company in the wake of her fellow celebrities: Rihanna's Fenty Beauty, Kylie Jenner's Kylie Cosmetics, Kim Kardashian's KKW Beauty, Jennifer Lopez's Inglot, Drew Barrymore's Flower Beauty, and celebrity beauty pioneer Jessica Alba's Honest Beauty.<!-- /react-text --></p>, <p class="article-paragraph" data-reactid="137"><!-- react-text: 138 -->Interestingly, Gaga might be taking cues mostly from Alba's venture, as Haus Beauty is reportedly being funded by The Honest Company's investment firm, Lightspeed Venture Partners, as Recode <!-- /react-text --><a data-reactid="139" href="https://www.recode.net/2018/7/12/17560196/lady-gaga-beauty-startup-haus-beauty-lightspeed-venture-honest-company">noted</a><!-- react-text: 140 -->. Plus, Haus Beauty is apparently being led by former Honest Company chief digital officer Ben Jones. (His LinkedIn entry confirms he left The Honest Company to become CEO at a "stealth" company.)<!-- /react-text --></p>, <p class="article-paragraph" data-reactid="141">What we don't know is how exactly Gaga will put her stamp on the celebrity beauty industry. Will her line embrace her maximal, costume-heavy early Gaga days? Or will it be rooted more in her minimal makeup (and Ally's no-makeup) look these days? Will it be as inclusive as her Born This Way Foundation? As usual, Gaga is leaving us guessing.</p>, <p class="tag-hed" data-reactid="162">Keywords</p>, <p class="dek" data-reactid="289">Stay connected.</p>, <p class="copyright-text" data-reactid="375"><!-- react-text: 376 -->\xa9 <!-- /react-text --><!-- react-text: 377 -->2019<!-- /react-text --><!-- react-text: 378 --> Cond\xe9 Nast. All rights reserved<!-- /react-text --></p>, <p class="legal-text" data-reactid="379"><!-- react-text: 380 -->Use of and/or registration on any portion of this site constitutes acceptance of our <!-- /react-text --><a class="link" data-reactid="381" href="https://www.condenast.com/privacy-policy" target="_self">User Agreement</a><!-- react-text: 382 --> (updated 5/25/18) and <!-- /react-text --><a class="link" data-reactid="383" href="https://www.condenast.com/privacy-policy#privacypolicy" target="_self">Privacy Policy and Cookie Statement</a><!-- react-text: 384 --> (updated 5/25/18).<!-- /react-text --></p>, <p class="legal-text" data-reactid="385"><em data-reactid="386">W Magazine</em><!-- react-text: 387 --> may earn a portion of sales from products that are purchased through our site as part of our Affiliate Partnerships with retailers.<!-- /react-text --><a class="link" data-reactid="388" href="https://www.condenast.com/privacy-policy#privacypolicy-california" target="_self">Your California Privacy Rights</a></p>, <p class="legal-text" data-reactid="389">The material on this site may not be reproduced, distributed, transmitted, cached or otherwise used, except with the prior written permission of Cond\xe9 Nast.</p>, <p class="legal-text" data-reactid="390"><a class="link" data-reactid="391" href="http://www.condenast.com/online-behavioral-advertising-oba-and-how-to-opt-out-of-oba/#clickheretoreadmoreaboutonlinebehavioraladvertising(oba)" target="_self">Ad Choices</a></p>]

[<p class="pfont-xsmall">\n<time content="2019-01-03" datetime="2019-01-03" itemprop="datePublished" pubdate="">\nThursday, 3 January 2019\n</time>\n- <a href="archive.cfm?sectionIs=news&amp;cat=Entertainment">Entertainment</a>\n</p>, <p>by <b itemprop="name">YA Reporter</b> - <span itemprop="jobTitle">YA Reporter</span></p>, <p class="pfont-small">Printed and digital download photos available</p>, <p class="pfont-lead" itemprop="description">1777: George Washington defeated the British at the Battle of Princeton.</p>, <p class="temp-fix-brad" itemprop="articleBody">1870: Work on the Brooklyn Bridge began.</p>, <p>1883: Clement Attlee, Labour Party leader and prime minister from 1945-51, was born.</p>, <p>1892: Author JRR Tolkien, creator of The Lord Of The Rings and The Hobbit, was born in South Africa. He died in Bournemouth in 1973.</p>, <p>1911: The Siege of Sidney Street took place when anarchists were besieged by police in a house in London\u2019s East End.</p>, <p>1924: English explorer Howard Carter discovered the sarcophagus of Tutankhamun in Egypt\u2019s Valley of Kings.</p>, <p>1946: Nazi propagandist William Joyce - the notorious Lord Haw-Haw - was hanged for treason.</p>, <p>1959: Alaska became the 49th state of America.</p>, <p>1961: The millionth Morris Minor, the highly successful British car designed by Sir Alec Issigonis, came off the assembly line at Oxford.</p>, <p>1997: The death toll in Europe\u2019s big freeze hit 220 as temperatures plunged to -10C from Britain to central Russia.</p>, <p>2009: Matt Smith was named as the new Doctor Who. He became the 11th Time Lord since the programme started in 1963.</p>, <p>ON THIS DAY LAST YEAR: The first polar bear cub born in the UK for 25 years was being monitored at a Scottish wildlife park.</p>, <p>BIRTHDAYS: Stephen Stills, rock singer, 74; John Paul Jones, rock musician (Led Zeppelin), 73; Mel Gibson, actor, 63; Gavin Hastings, rugby great, 57; Michael Schumacher, former racing driver, 50; Dominic Wood, children\u2019s television presenter, 41.</p>, <p>Geoffrey H...</p>, <p>Tue:\t0256\t6.20\t1523 6.20</p>, <p>Wed:\t0329\t6.00\t1600\t6.00</p>, <p>Thur...</p>, <p>Geoffrey H...</p>, <p class="pfont-small">Ask about advertising on our websites</p>, <p class="pfont-small">Digital or printed subscriptions</p>, <p class="pfont-small">Have a story you want to share?</p>, <p class="pfont-small">Development plans in your area</p>, <p class="pfont-small">Start the search for your new career</p>, <p class="pfont-small">Weather updates in your region</p>, <p class="pfont-small">Watch our local news video</p>, <p class="pfont-small">Order photos from our newspaper</p>, <p class="pfont-small">You could reach more customers with our print and online ad packages.</p>, <p class="pfont-small"><strong>Independent Family-Owned Newspapers</strong>\n\xb7\nCopyright &amp; Trade Mark Notice &amp; 2013 - 2019 <br>Owned or licensed to <a href="http://www.tindlenews.co.uk">Tindle Newspapers Ltd.</a> \xb7 <a href="terms.cfm">T &amp; C</a> \xb7 <a href="privacy.cfm">Privacy Policy</a> \xb7 <a href="complaints.cfm">Complaints</a> \xb7 <a href="javascript:window.cmpConfig.methods.summon()">Review Consent Preferences</a></br></p>]
[<p class="SiteHeader__title___aZr3Q"></p>, <p class="Byline__by___37lv8">By <a class="Link__link___3dWao " href="/contributors/troy-patterson" rel="author" title="Troy Patterson">Troy Patterson</a></p>, <p class="ArticleTimestamp__timestamp___1klks ">4:29 P.M.</p>, <p>\u201cTidying Up,\u201d which grafts Marie Kondo\u2019s methodology onto a makeover-show format, does not offer much struggle or conflict; instead, her mere presence initiates self-directed journeys.</p>, <p>Netflix <span data-page="page_1"></span>dropped \u201cTidying Up with Marie Kondo,\u201d on January 1st, to serve viewers\u2019 urges of self-improvement at the start of the New Year. The show\u2019s optimistic visions of revitalization, achieved through simple efforts toward domestic order, is a decent hangover sedative in itself. Our host is the author of the best-selling self-help guide \u201c<a class="ArticleBody__link___1FS03" href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/1607747308/?tag=thneyo0f-20" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">The Life-Changing Magic of Tidying Up: The Japanese Art of Decluttering and Organizing</a>.\u201d In each of the season\u2019s eight episodes, Kondo materializes in a home to bless it with her practical philosophy of purging junk. \u201cI love a mess,\u201d she says. She likes a challenge, that is. Each episode of this housekeeping procedural preaches the pleasures of her process. I found it impossible to binge the show, largely because it kept jolting me to the back of the closet in the kids\u2019 room, where I meditated on disused Hot Wheels race tracks.</p>, <p>The introduction finds the petite Kondo approaching an overstuffed closet, daintily hopping to reach a high shelf, and cutely failing. There is perhaps a smidgen of Orientalism in the series\u2019s framing of its Japanese star as a sprite who flutters efficiently across a nonspecific U.S.A., gracing its chaotic households with wisdom. Perhaps she\u2019s not an Other, just otherworldly, in the manner of a fairy godmother or enchanted nanny. Either way, spirituality is essential to her method, and \u201cmagic\u201d is central to its meaning; she knows that the unloved stuff in the garage is weighing down the soul. The word \u201ctidying,\u201d with its implication of light dusting and fluffing sofa cushions, is insufficient to the physical task Kondo proposes, which may involve gathering an entire wardrobe of clothing, accumulated over decades, into a linebacker-size pile. This is a vision of the organizational consultant as a freelance exorcist. In its formulation of these tasks not as tedious chores but as energizing exercises, it is in line with current discourse on self-care, in which moisturizing lotions are sacramental ointments.</p>, <p>A typical episode of \u201cTidying Up,\u201d which grafts Kondo\u2019s methodology onto a familiar makeover-show format, does not offer much in the way of struggle or conflict. Kondo\u2019s mere presence initiates self-directed journeys, and her thorough pleasantness closes off the possibility of \u201cSupernanny\u201d-type scoldings. The sensibility of the production accidentally casts complicated problems as jokes. A black-and-white sequence depicting the frustration of a guy who despairs that his toddlers are \u201cgetting the worst of me\u201d finds him venting at his wife. \u201cThere are seven pillows on this bed,\u201d he fumes, \u201cand <em class="">those aren\u2019t even decorative pillows</em>.\u201d The soundtrack simpers along with the generic jangling guitar and mawkish plinking piano of any given HGTV program, but it flips to something chiming and ethereal when Kondo appears alone, in a vaguely celestial setting, addressing the viewer directly in instructional interludes.</p>, <p>Kondo, of course, has a million-dollar catchphrase: initiates must cast out items that fail to \u201cspark joy.\u201d (According to this principle, I chucked my household\u2019s copy of \u201cLife-Changing Magic\u201d after a half hour\u2019s perusal of its welcome advice.) \u201cWhen you touch the item that sparks joy for you, you feel <em class="">chi-i-ing</em>\xa0.\xa0.\xa0. all of yourself rising,\u201d Kondo says, in the first episode. When she issues that sound effect\u2014a noise onomatopoeic of crystalline cheer\u2014her voice and smile gleam like a glass in a dish-detergent ad. It\u2019s unspeakably charming. But the laws of brand extension decree that she must keep renewing and reinterpreting the phrase. The buzzword becomes a nagging drone, and related themes are repeated until they begin to sound like nonsense. Knowing that sentimental attachments can be shackles, Kondo directs her clients to fill their hearts with gratitude for items that have outlived their utility. (An expired packet of gravy mix cannot bear this degree of reverence, but that\u2019s neither here nor there.) The show is decent company if you\u2019re just sitting there folding the laundry, and you will be folding it with unprecedented panache\u2014conveying \u201clove to your clothes from the palms of your hands,\u201d Kondo says\u2014if you follow her teachings. \u201cTidying Up\u201d is mindless television on the topic of mindful domesticity.</p>, <p class="ArticleContributors__contributorBioText___3m1QB">Troy Patterson is a staff writer at The New Yorker.</p>, <p class="NewsletterSubscribe__newsletterDek___29WDu">Sign up for the <i>New Yorker</i> [<p class="forget-name-link pull-left">\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tForgot <a href="#">\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tUsername</a> or <a href="#">\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tPassword</a>\n</p>, <p id="ContentPlaceHolder1_author_section"></p>, <p class="author"> <a href="#" rel="author" title="Posts by NewEdge">Date</a></p>, <p>\r\n                 (MENAFN - PRLog) The Whiteboard Challenge Game Show is scheduled to film its pilot episode on Saturday April 27, 2019 at Cross Campus in Downtown Los Angeles from 2pm to 5pm. <br/> <br/> The Whiteboard Challenge Game Show is a revolutionary game show taking aim at the tech-industry's interview process. With decades of experience in the industry, Michael Kureth envisioned a game show that would introduce the masses to what actually happens in the interview conference rooms of top tech companies. <br/> <br/> Three contestants will have the chance to impress the judges, all tech-industry insiders, for a chance to show off their technical prowess both on the whiteboard and in a timed coding event. With a set of tokens, players will be able to change the outcome of their own whiteboard session while hindering that of their colleagues. <br/> <br/> Filmed in Los Angeles in front of a live audience of industry professionals, contestants compete for prizes and recognition. Being crowned champion labels one contestant as the true "rockstar" above all in an over saturated tech industry where everyone is claiming to be a software engineer. <br/> <br/> To guarantee seating for professionals and avoid interruptions, we kindly ask that no recruiters attend the event. <br/> <br/> IMDB: https://www.imdb.com/title/tt9470306/ <br/> Site: http://WhiteboardChallenge.com <br/> <br/> <div> Contact <br/> Michael Kureth <br/> ***@whiteboardchallenge.com <br/> <br/> Photo: <br/> https://www.prlog.org/12746823/1 </div> <div></div><p>MENAFN0301201900703076ID1097920885</p><!--MENAFN0301201900703076ID1097920885--></p>, <p>MENAFN0301201900703076ID1097920885</p>, <p></p>, <p>Tags</p>, <p>Comments</p>, <p>Category</p>, <p>Date</p>, <p class="footer-info">\n<div class="radio">\n<label><input checked="" name="question" type="radio" value="0"/> Daily English </label>\n</div>\n<div class="radio">\n<label><input name="question" type="radio" value="1"/> Daily Arabic </label>\n</div>\n<div class="radio">\n<label><input name="question" type="radio" value="2"/> All </label>\n</div>\n</p>, <p class="footer-logo"><img alt="logo" src="/includes/img/logo.jpg"/></p>, <p class="footer-info" style="font:15px;">World and Middle East business and financial news, Stocks, Currencies, Market Data, Research, Weather and other data.</p>, <p style="display:table-row;">\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t Contact Us\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span style="font-size:16px;color:White;font-weight:bold;padding-left: 5px;"><a href="https://menafn.com/mf_contact.aspx?src=Contact_Gen"> Click here </a></span>\n</p>, <p>\n<span>Tel:</span>\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t+962 6 5690450\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</p>, <p class="copyright">\r\n                        Copyright \xa9 2000 <a href="https://menafn.com">MENAFN.</a> All rights reserved.</p>, <p class="pull-right">\r\n                        Design &amp; Devleopment by\xa0<a href="https://menafn.com/">MENAFN</a></p>]
